Jamison Brereton

18 (459)
Indra
Bharadv─Бja B─Бrhaspatya
15 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
The poet of this hymn seems to be aiming to deploy as many different words for power, might, strength, and so forth in as many different derivational forms as pos sible. The sheer power of Indra, thus expressed, overshadows his particular deeds, which are mentioned in a somewhat cursory way: Vala (vs. 5), Vr╠еtra (vs. 6, also 9 and 14), the destruction of various named monsters (vs. 8). The poet is also fond of figures involving a positive and a twist on its negation: тАЬvanquishing but unvan quishedтАЭ (vs. 1), and so forth.
This focus on IndraтАЩs power betrays some nervous worry about the existence of that power, expressed especially in the rhetorical question and answer in verses 3тАУ4. A number of hymns in the R╠еgveda raise the question of whether Indra himself exists; here the existential anxiety has been displaced to an abstract entity, his might, but the poet asserts its existence so often and so unequivocally that his audience can scarcely doubt it. Needless to say, the recital of IndraтАЩs strength is not disinter ested: the poet calls for Indra to use his powers in defense of the poetтАЩs people and, in the last verse (15), to perform the deed that exists for him to do (a nice return to the existential theme), in order to merit another poem from the poet.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPraise him who is Indra, the invoker of many, endowed with overpowering vigour, the destroyer (of foes), unharmed by them; exalt with these praises the irresistible, fierce, victorious Indra, the showerer (of benefits) upon mankind.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Praise him whose might is overpowering, the vanquishing but
unvanquished, much-summoned Indra.
Mighty, conquering but unconquered, the bull of the settled domainsтАФ strengthen him with these songs.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. contains two pairs of positive/negative etymological figures, both consisting of a pres. participle with тАЬactiveтАЭ value (though one of them is morphologically middle) and a negated past part.: vanv├бnn ├бv─Бtaс╕е тАЬvanquishing but unvanquishedтАЭ and ├бс╣г─Бс╕╖ham тАж s├бham─Бnam тАЬconquering but unconquered.тАЭ It may not be an accident that the root syllables in each pair, though related by standard derivational processes, are quite distinct because of morphophonemic changes: van / v─Б and sah / с╣г─Бс╕╖h.

Griffith

GLORIFY him whose might is all-surpassing, Indra the much-invoked who fights uninjured.
Magnify with these songs the never-vanquished, the Strong, the Bull of men, the Mighty Victor.

Den Indra preise, der von hoher Kraft ist, und ungef├дhrdet siegreich, vielgerufen, Den unbesiegten Sieger, den gewalt’gen, mit diesen Liedern st├дrk den Herrn der Menschen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe is ever the combatant, the donor, the engaged in battle, the sympathizer (with the sacrificer), the benefactor of many, the loud-sounding, the partaker of the stale libation, the stirrer up of dust (in strife), the chief protector of men the descendants of Manu, the endowed with strength.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

HeтАФthe fighting warrior, creator of tumult, combat-hardened, the powerfully destructive, bellowing partaker of the silvery drink,
with high-mounting dustтАФalone became the victorious rouser of the communities of the sons of Manu.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On unclear khaja- see comm. ad VII.20.3.

Griffith

He, Champion, Hero, Warrior, Lord of battles, impetuous, loudly roaring, great destroyer,
Who whirls the dust on high, alone, oerthrower, hath made all races of mankind his subjects.

Geldner

Dieser kampfge├╝bte Soldat, streitbar, schlachtgewohnt, viele aufreibend, l├дrmend, den Trestersaft trinkend, bei dem der Staub hoch geht, er ward der alleinige sieghafte Aufr├╝ttler der menschlichen V├╢lker.

Grassmann

Der tapfre K├дmpfer, Schlacht erregend, streitbar, der viele tilgt, wild tobend vorw├дrts dringet, Er, Staub aufwirbelnd, war allein der starke Ersch├╝tterer der menschlichen Geschlechter.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou are he who has quickly humbled the Dasyus; you are the chief one who has given posterity to the Arya;but, Indra, is not verily your power such? If it be not, then in due season confess.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Not beholding Indra, the с╣Ыс╣гi began to question his attributes and power; next verse explains his belief in these attributes and power

Jamison Brereton

It was just you who tamed the Dasyus, and who alone vanquished (their) communities for the ─Аrya.
Does that heroic power now exist for you, Indra, or does it not? You will announce that at the proper season.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The sequence 2ND SG. PRN ha ty├бd (here ha n├║ ty├бd) is fairly common and appears to be strongly emphatic, hence my tr. тАЬit was just youтАЭ (etc.). In several hymns (I.63.4-7, VIII.96.16-18) this construction is found in series. I take the fronted ├бsti followed by svid to be a strong existential тАЬdoes it exist?тАЭ rather than simply the possessive constr. that Geldner sees: тАЬHast du тАж diese Manneskrafte тАж?тАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYet, most mighty one, I believe that powre is verily always in you, who are manifest at many rites, and are the enemy of (our) enemies; (the power) that is fierce in the fierce one, most mighty in the mighty one, most unassailable in the subduer (of foes).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

It certainly does exist for you!тАФso I think: strength, o strongest one, (has come) to you, who were powerfully born, the surpassing surpasserтАФ mighty (strength) has come to the mighty one, more powerful (strength) to the powerful one who, himself not feeble, furthers the feeble.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The fronted ├бsti in the previous vs. is matched by equally emphatic, fronted s├бd ├нd. Although Geldner takes s├бt as the modifier of the s├бhaс╕е that begins the next p─Бda, I think instead that it answers the question posed in 3cd and therefore implicitly modifies v─лry├аm in 3c. This is then further specified as s├бhaс╕е beginning in b, which then is qualified by the adjectives ugr├бm and t├бv─лyaс╕е in c.

The last three p─Бdas of the vs. are a veritable riot of etymological figures, with two each in b and c and one in d: b s├бhaс╕е sahiс╣гс╣нha turat├бs tur├бsya, c ugr├бm ugr├бsya tav├бsas t├бv─лyaс╕е, d ├бradhrasya radhrat├║raс╕е тАж The 2nd member of this last cmpd, -tur-, belongs etymologically with the 2nd figure of b, turat├бs tur├бsya, though unfortunately since itтАЩs used in a somewhat different sense, this connection cannot easily be conveyed in translation. Similarly, the 2nd figure of c, tav├бsas t├бv─лyaс╕е, picks up the tuvi- of the cmpd in a, tuvi-j─Бt├б-. So, in addition to the juxtaposed linear figures, there is some interweaving across p─Бda boundaries.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay that our ancient friendship with you ever endure; as when, along with the Aс╣Еgirasas, celebrating your praises, you, beautiful Indra, caster down of the immoveable (roks), did verily slay Bala, hurling (his darts against you), and force open his cities, and all his gates.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

тАЬLet our age-old partnership with you (all) (still) exist,тАЭ with the Aс╣Еgirases speaking in just this wayтАФalong with them
you smashed the prospering Vala cave, o wondrous shaker of the
unshakable, and you opened its strongholds and its doors, all of them.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As the opening words of p─Бda b, itth─Б╠Бv├бdadbhiс╕е, indicate, the previous p─Бda is the direct speech of the Aс╣Еgirases. In keeping with the two immediately preceding vss., I take astu as an existential: тАЬlet that partnership (still) exist.тАЭ The wording is otherwise very like IV.10.8 ┼Ыiv─Б╠Бnaс╕е sakhy─Б╠Бs├бntu … dev├йс╣гu yuс╣гm├й. The clear loc. dev├йс╣гu in that passage anchors the loc. identity of yuс╣гm├й both in that passage and this one. The loc. is somewhat odd: generally sakhy├б- is construed with gen. or instr., as already set forth by Grassmann s.v. However, cf. VII.22.9 (=X.23.7), which also contains a pl.

ps. prn. in -e: asm├й te santu sakhy─Б╠Б┼Ыiv─Б╠Бni. In the published translation I take the asm├й there as a dat.: тАЬLet there be friendly fellowship of you for us.тАЭ But in light of the two parallel structures with yuс╣гm├й, I think it must be a loc., and these three passages, each of which is rendered differently in the published translation, should be harmonized. I now think that all three are existential (although the two with ┼Ыiv├б- could be equational, with a pred.

adj.) and that the loc. specifies the locus of the partnership, either in or тАЬbeiтАЭ the pronominal referent. Though this is functionally equivalent to тАЬwith,тАЭ as in the published

tr., I would slightly modify the tr. to better reflect the loc.: тАЬLet there (still) be ageold partnership for us among you,тАЭ though тАЬтАж with youтАЭ would in fact be clearer.

The placement of val├бm in the middle of the instr. phrase in b, with its governing verb (h├бn) not found till c, is somewhat odd, but see comm. ad vs. 8 below.

Presumably the Vala cave is тАЬprosperingтАЭ because it is full of cows. On the accent of iс╣г├бyantam here, see my -├бya-Formations, p. 49 and n. 3.

The positive active / negative passive figure found twice in vs. 1 is here embodied in the single word, the root-noun cmpd voc. acyuta-cyut- тАШshaker of the unshakableтАЩ.

Griffith

Be this our ancient bond of friendship with you and with Angirases here who speak of Vala.
Thou, Wondrous, Shaker of things firm, didst smite him in his fresh strength, and force his doors and castles.

Geldner

Das soll unsere alte Freundschaft mit euch sein", mit den ebenso sprechenden Angiras┬┤ erschlugest du den die K├╝he genie├Яenden Vala, du das Unbewegliche bewegende Meister. Du schlossest seine Burgen, alle seine Tore auf.

Grassmann

Es sei mit euch uns diese alte Freundschaft; von Angiras besungen, schlugst, o hehrer, Den kr├дft’gen Vala du, o Allersch├╝ttrer, erschlossest seine Burgen all und Th├╝ren.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬFierce Indra, maker of rules you are he who is to be invoked with praise in a great conflict; you are he (who is to be invoked) for sons and grandsons, he, the wielder of the thunderbolt, who is to be especially glorified in battles.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He is to be summoned with insightful thoughtsтАФthe mighty one who performs the masterтАЩs part in the great overcoming of Vr╠еtra,
in the winning of progeny, in (the winning of) posterity. As the
mace-bearer he became worth tussling for in battles.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The vs. contains 3 coreferential s├б, at the beg. of a and of c and in the middle of c. I have interpr. the first half of c as belonging with ab, with the loc. tok├бs─Бt─Б t├бnaye parallel to loc. mahat├н vс╣Ыtrat┼л╠Бrye in b and the mid-p─Бda s├б in c introducing a new cl. Others (Geldner, Schaef., Intens. 126) take all of c with d. There is no way to determine and very little riding on it. However, see the comm. on the next vs. The h├н in p─Бda a seems to have little or no causal value; similarly the one in 4a.

Although the overt ├бsti reminds us of the other overt forms of тИЪas in previous vss. (3, 4, 5), which were (at least by my lights) existential, ├бsti here seems to be a straight copula and therefore pleonastic+++(=redundant)+++.

In tok├бs─Бt─Б t├бnaye we can assume that t├бnaye shows a kind of gapping of the 2nd cmpd member found in tok├б-s─Бti-, hence a putative *t├бnaya-s─Бti-. GeldnerтАЩs cited parallels, e.g., II.30.5 tok├бsya s─Бta├║ t├бnayasya тАж, confirm this.

Griffith

With holy thoughts must he be called, the Mighty, showing his power in the great fight with Vrtra.
He must be called to give us seed and offspring, the Thunderer must he moved and sped to battle.

Geldner

Denn er ist mit Gebeten anzurufen, der Gewaltige, der Reichmacher, in der gro├Яen Feindeschlacht; er ward bei der Gewinnung von Samen, von leiblicher Nachkommenschaft, der Keulentr├дger in den Schlachten, der, um den man sich rei├Яt.

Grassmann

Denn durch Gebet l├дsst sich erflehn der hehre, der Herrschaft ├╝bt im grossen Vritrakampfe, Dass Kind und Enkel wir erlangen, ist er, der Blitzende, in Schlachten herzulocken.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWith immortal, foe-humiliating might he has promoted the (multiplied) birth of mankind; he, the chief of leaders, dwells in the same dwelling with fame, with strength, with riches, with heroism.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Through his greatness and his immortal name he has extended himself over the races of the sons of Manu.
He is at home with brilliance and with power and wealth, and he, the best of men, with heroismтАФ

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. continues the overabundance of s├б from the last vs., esp. in the 2nd hemistich, with initial s├б and post-caesura s├б in c and initial s├б in d, in addition to the one opening the vs. Each of these s├б is associated with a different instr. phrase or phrases. The one in the first hemistich has the capacious bipartite majm├бn─Б тАж ├бmartyena n─Б╠Бmn─Б embedded in a full clause with the verb pr├б sarsre; the two in p─Бda c occur only with instrumentals (dyumn├йna in the opening and the conjoined ┼Ы├бvasot├б r─Бy─Б╠Бafter the caesura); the one in d has only a single instr. (v─лry├ис╣Зa) but is part of a clause again, though with a pred. adj. s├бmokaс╕е, not a finite verb. Since the structure of this vs. is like that of vs. 6, the question again arises as to where to attach c (or the two parts of c). Flg. Geldner I take all of c with d, construing all the instrumentals with s├бmokaс╕е тАШat home (with)тАЩ. But I now see that, because the structures in c are minimal, it could as well go with ab (or the first half with ab, the second with d). This would produce alternative translations тАЬThrough his greatness and his immortal name he extended himself, (and also) through his brilliance and his power and wealth. He is at home with heroism.тАЭ or even тАЬThrough his greatness and his immortal name he extended himself, (and also) through his brilliance; he is at home with power and wealth and with heroism.тАЭ (This last, with the first part of c leaning backward and the 2nd leaning forward, would mimic my interpr. of vs. 6.) Again I do not see a way to decide the question, but I think itтАЩs worth noting how the poet has cleverly constructed p─Бda c so that it is ambig.

Griffith

He in his might, with name that lives for ever, hath far surpassed all human generations.
He, most heroic, hath his home with splendour, with glory and with riches and with valour.

Geldner

Mit seiner M├дchtigkeit, seinem unsterblichen Namen ├╝berdauert er der Menschen Geschlechter. Er ist mit Glanz, mit Kraft und Reichtum, er mit Heldenmut gepaart, der Mannhafteste.

Er dringt mit Macht hindurch durch die Geschlechter der Menschen mit unsterblichem Erscheinen, Mit sch├╢nem Gut, mit St├дrke und mit Reichthum, mit Heldenkraft gepaart der m├дnnlich st├дrkste,

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe who is never perplexed, who is no engenderer of that which is in vain, whose name is renowned, who promptly (exerts himself) for the overturning of the cities (of the asuras), and for the destruction (of his foes); you, (Indra), have indeed slain Cumuri, Dhuni, Pipru, ┼Ъambara, and ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He, the man who is not to be confused and is not wrong, bearing a name that is good to think upon. Cumuri and Dhuni
did Indra wring out, and Pipru, ┼Ъambara, and ┼Ъuс╣гс╣ЗaтАФto shake their strongholds and for (them) to lie there even now.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Geldner points out (n. 8b), the role of Cumuri and Dhuni in the RV is to be put to sleep by Indra, so that Dabh─лti can deliver the coup de gr├вce to them. See the various passages adduced by Geldner and esp. nearby VI.26.6. In our vs. they are marooned at the end of the first hemistich, and after an initial verb in c another set of IndraтАЩs victims is introduced: Pipru, ┼Ъambara, and ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa. Geldner asks whether we should assume an ellipsis with Cumuri/Dhuni phrase (in other words, supply a form of тАЬput to sleepтАЭ) or a zeugma (in other words, to take them as objects of vс╣Ыс╣З├бk with the Pipru group, though their fates were met in different ways). I have chosen the 2nd option. The audience would certainly know the particular destiny of Cumuri and Dhuni but would also be able to lump them in with other targets of Indra, all as objects of a generically violent verb. (It may be worth noting that vс╣Ыn├бk here is one of the very few forms of тИЪvс╣Ыj that lacks a preverb, though cf. nearby VI.26.3.) The segregation of Cumuri and Dhuni in p─Бda b, away from the verb and the other victims, might give us pause, but cf. vs. 5, where the obj. val├бm is found in the interior of p─Бda b, with the verb beginning c.

In d the datives cyautn─Б╠Бya and ┼Ыay├бth─Бya have parallel infinitival function.

For the latter cf. also ┼Ыay├бthe in the preceding hymn (VI.17.9, with disc. ad loc.) with the same apparent meaning but in a different case.

Griffith

Stranger to guile, who ne’er was false or faithless, bearing a name that may be well remembered,
Indra crushed Cumuri, Dhuni, Sambara, Pipru, and Susna, that their castles fell in ruin.

Geldner

Er, der nicht der Mann ist, welcher irren oder fehlen kann, dessen Namens man gern gedenkt, er hat den Cumuri und Dhuni - Indra rang mit Pipru, Sambara, Susna, um die Burgen zu ersch├╝ttern, da├Я sie f├╝r immer daliegen.

Grassmann

Zu schrecken nicht ist er, der Mann, noch falsch er, der wohlbekannte Indra st├╝rzte Dhuni Und Tschumuri, ├Зambara, Pipru, ├Зuschna zur Burgzerschmettrung, ew’ger Niederlage.

тАЬ(Endowed) with upward-rising, foe-thinning, and glorified (vigour), ascend your car for the destruction of Vс╣Ыtra; take the thunderbolt in your right hand, giver of wealth, baffle the devices (of the asuras).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

With your helpful energy, (ever) more to be admired, up and mount your chariot, Indra, for the Vr╠еtra-smashing.
Place your mace in your hand on the right side. Stimulate your magical powers, o you who give much.

Jamison Brereton Notes

ud─Б╠Бvat─Б is read ud├бvat─Б by the Pp. and is generally considered the instr. of the pres. act. part. of ├║d тИЪav тАШhelpтАЩ, with metrical lengthening (so explicitly Lubotsky), a lengthening that is unmotivated. It is also the case that ├║d is not especially common with тИЪav, though I concede that the six passages IтАЩm aware of make this an established usage. I also find it surprising that there is no preverb with tiс╣гс╣нha in the expression in b, r├бtham тАж tiс╣гс╣нha тАЬmount the chariot,тАЭ since this expression is almost always found with preverb, generally ─Б╠Б, also ├бdhi. I therefore wonder if the initial string in p─Бda a is actually concealing the preverb(s), in tmesis: ud-─Б╠Б, followed by the uncompounded pres. part. ├бvat─Б. This analysis is responsible for my tr. тАЬup and mount тАжтАЭ I realize, however, that a number of objections can be raised. The combination ud-─Б╠БdoesnтАЩt otherwise occur with тИЪsth─Б, but I would point out that both occur with that root individually. Two further potential problems: 1) two preverbs next to each other in tmesis, rather than the usual single one. I confess I do not know of other examples. 2) the accentuation: the accented vowels of ─Б╠Бand ├бvat─Б would coalesce, resulting in a single ud─Бtta – this is unproblematic – but the lack of accent on ud looms larger. Here I rely on MacdonellтАЩs observation (VGS, p. 469) that when ─Б╠Бis immediately preceded by another preverb, ─Б╠Бalone has the accent. In MacdonellтАЩs formulation this applies (only) to these sequences when compounded with verbs; I would here extend that to the same sequence in tmesis. This may be too much machinery to deploy simply in order to account for the surprising, supposed metrical lengthening of ud─Б╠Бvat─Б and the surprising lack of preverb with tiс╣гс╣нha, but it seems worth considering. Alternatively, it could be that ud─Б╠Бvat─Б is a cmpded pres. part., but cmpded not only with ├║d, but also ─Б╠Б. This is the solution of Rivelex (I.541), and it may be the best compromise, though ─Б╠Бis not otherwise found with тИЪav, as far as I know. (I have not been able to find the ─Б╠Б+тИЪav claimed by Rivelex in the head note on p. 538, and in the claimed pr├б ─Б╠Бpassage (VIII.23.2), ─Б╠Бis a postposition, as is more or less admitted p. 543 n. 1.) The ca in the instr. phrase in p─Бda a seems pleonastic+++(=redundant)+++, and if it is implicitly connecting the two adj. modifying tv├бkс╣гas─Б, viz. ├бvat─Б (or ud─Б╠Бvat─Б) and p├бnyas─Б (Klein DGRV I.71 тАЬaiding and wondrousтАЭ), they seem ill-assorted semantically. I wonder if it is meant to connect the first ADJ.-NOUN pair with a 2nd, with gapping of the noun modified by p├бnyas─Б (тАЬwith your helpful energy and ever more admirable XтАЭ). But there is no standard p├бnyas- NOUN formula, so I will not pursue this.

In d Oldenberg (Noten) and Geldner assume that the m─Бy─Б╠Бс╕е are negative magical wiles that belong to IndraтАЩs opponents. A negative valuation of m─Бy─Б╠Б- is of course common, and is clear in the nearby passage VI.22.9, where a p─Бda almost identical to our c, urging Indra to take his mace in hand, precedes one in which he is urged to destroy m─Бy─Б╠Бс╕е (VI.22.9cd dhiс╣гv├б v├бjraс╣Г d├бkс╣гiс╣Зa indra h├бste, v├н┼Ыv─Б ajurya dayase v├н m─Бy─Б╠Бс╕е) -

  • though see comm. ad loc: a secondary positive reading is also possible. This parallel is an important piece of evidence for both OldenbergтАЩs and GeldnerтАЩs assessment of m─Бy─Б╠Бс╕е here. However, this reasonable interpr. ignores one major factor in our passage: the verb abh├н pr├б manda. This lexeme occurs a number of times elsewhere (V.4.1, VII.33.1, VIII.12.13, 93.19), and it is always otherwise positive: act.

тАШexhilarateтАЩ, mid. тАШbecome exhilaratedтАЩ. A negative interpr. of m─Бy─Б╠Бс╕е requires a serious distortion of the meaning of the verb (e.g., OldenbergтАЩs тАШverwirrenтАЩ, adopted from BR), whereas assuming the m─Бy─Б╠Бс╕е belong to Indra allows it to have a small extension of its usual sense: тАШexhilarateтАЩ ├а тАШstimulateтАЩ. Just as soma exhilarates and stimulates Indra for the Vс╣Ыtra-smashing, so does Indra exhilarate and stimulate his own powers.

Oldenberg in fact previously (ZDMG 55.323) made a good case that the m─Бy─Б╠Бс╕е are IndraтАЩs, third in a list of his Kampfmittel that includes the chariot of b and the mace of c, and he suggested a tr. тАЬSetze deine Wunderkr├дfte in freudige ErregungтАЭ very much like mine. He attributes his change of heart in the Noten to VI.22.9 just cited and to his consideration of тАЬDer Gesamteindruck des Auftretens von m─Бy─Б╠Бс╕е in den Indraliedern.тАЭ But, in fact, he overlooked one very crucial occurrence, in this very hymn: in vs. 12 Indra himself is called purum─Бy├б- тАШhaving many magical powersтАЩ (cf. also nearby VI.21.2 and 22.1 in this same Indra cycle, also III.51.4). This seems to me clinching evidence against the Geldner/Oldenberg interpr. of our d: Indra has many m─Бy─Б╠Б- and he deploys them to achieve his ends. (Got┼Н [1st Kl., 236 n. 521] finds the passage puzzling, but does try to reconcile it with the usage of the verb, not entirely successfully.)

рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реНрди рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░рд┐рд╡ ред рдирд╢рдмреНрдж рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд░реНрдереАрдпрдГ ред рдпрдерд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рд╢реБрд╖реНрдХрдВ рдиреАрд░рд╕рдВ рд╡рдирдВ рд╡реГрдХреНрд╖рд╕рдореВрд╣рдВ рджрд╣рддрд┐ рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рд╣реЗрддрд┐рдГ рддреНрд╡рджреАрдпрдВ рд╡рдЬреНрд░рдВ рддрджреНрд╡рдЪреНрдЫрддреНрд░реВрдиреН рдирд╛рд╢рдпрддрд┐ ред рддрджреЗрд╡рд╛рд╣ ред рдЕрд╢рдирд┐рд░реНрди рднреАрдорд╛ ред рдпрдерд╛рд╢рдирд┐рд░реНрднреАрдорд╛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рджреНрднрдпрдВрдХрд░рд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдГ рд░рд╛рдХреНрд╖рд╕рдВ рдирд┐ рдзрдХреНрд╖рд┐ рд╡рдЬреНрд░реЗрдг рдирд┐рддрд░рд╛рдВ рджрд╣ ред рдпрдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдЧрдореНрднреАрд░рдпрд╛ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрднрд┐рд░рдзрд░реНрд╖рдгреАрдпрдпрд╛ рдЛрд╖реНрд╡рдпрд╛ рдорд╣рддреНрдпрд╛ ред рдЕрд╢реНрд╡ рдЗрддрд┐ рдорд╣рдиреНрдирд╛рдореИрддрддреН ред рд╣реЗрддреНрдпрд╛ рд░реБрд░реЛрдЬ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рдмрднрдЮреНрдЬред рдЕрдзреНрд╡рдирдпрддреН рдпреБрджреНрдзреЗ рдЧрд░реНрдЬрдирд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдВ рд╢рдмреНрджрдВ рдХрд░реЛрддрд┐ рдЪ ред рддрдерд╛ рджреБрд░рд┐рддрд╛ рджреБрд░рд┐рддрд╛рдирд┐ рджрдореНрднрдпрдЪреНрдЪ рднрд┐рдирддреНрддрд┐ рдЪ ред рд╕ рддреНрд╡рдВ рд░рдХреНрд╖реЛ рдирд┐ рдзрдХреНрд╖реАрддрд┐ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЗрдгрд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ рее рее рел рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIn like manner as Agni consumes the dry forest, so, Indra, your weapon (destroys your enemies); as (formidable as you) fearful shaft, consume the r─Бkс╣гasas; you who have shouted aloud (in the combat) and demolished all evil things.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

As fire does dry wood, like a terrifying missile burn down the demon with your lance, o Indra.
He who shattered the obstacles to progress with a (lance) both deep and high, he smoked them out and subjugated them.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The imagery is somewhat mixed here: it is hard to see how either a missile (nom. a┼Ы├бniс╕е) or a lance (instr. het─л╠Б[contra Pp. het├нс╕е, as seen already by Grassmann etc.]) can burn down anything. I assume itтАЩs a transferred visual image from the fire simile, since flames can have a lance-like shape and shoot out dramatically.

The fem. instr. adj. phrase gambh─лr├бya с╣Ыс╣гv├бy─Б lacks an overt referent. Geldner supplies Stimme without disc. In the absence of any obvious choices, I follow Grassmann in assuming het─л╠Бfrom p─Бda b. Neither с╣Ыс╣гv├б- nor gambh─лr├б- has a standard fem. referent.

The obj. of rur├│ja is likewise unexpressed. Geldner supplies Burgen (p├║raс╕е, a common obj. of this verb), but (n. 10cd) suggests that r├бkс╣гaс╕е from b is also possible.

Since the y├│ rur├│ja rel. clause of c is picked up by the main cl. of d, I instead supply durit─Б╠Б, which is the obj. of the conjoined verbs of d. Elsewhere durit─Б╠Бis the obj. of тИЪhan (IX.62.2, 90.6, 97.16), a verb semantically similar to тИЪruj.

Griffith

As Agni, as the dart burns the dry forest, like the dread shaft burn down the fiends, O Indra;
Thou who with high deep-reaching spear hast broken, hast covered over mischief and destroyed it.

Geldner

Wie das Feuer das trockene Geh├╢lz, so brenn, o Indra, mit deinem Gescho├Я den b├╢├Яen Geist nieder, wie der furchtbare Blitzstrahl! Er, der die Burgen mit dumpfer, mit hoher Stimme gebrochen hat, er r├дucherte die Schlupfwinkel aus und ├╝berrumpelte sie.

Grassmann

Wie Glut das d├╝rre Holz, verbrenn, o Indra, wie grauser Blitz mit heissem Speer die Geister, Der du mit hohem Spiess, der tief hinabreicht, Unheil zerbrachst, austilgtest und zerst├╢rtest.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOpulent, Indra, son of strength, the invoker of many, whose union (with energy) the impious is unable to disjoint, come down to us with thousands of riches by very powerful conveyances.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Potobhistuvi v─Бjebhiс╕е: i.e. v─Бhaiс╕е, vehicles, or sometimes horses; the epithet is: b─Бhubalaiс╕е, very storng or powerful

Jamison Brereton

Along a thousand paths affording powerful prizes, o powerfully brilliant Indra, drive here in our direction with wealth,
o much summoned son of strength, whom a godless man never has the power to repel.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Grassmann takes the referent of y├бsya as тАШwealthтАЩ (see col. 1114, s.v. y├│tu-). But it is far more likely that it is Indra, whom we are urging to come here – and whose arrival might be threatened by the actions of the ungodly man. (It is not possible to determine from GeldnerтАЩs tr. (тАЬdenтАЭ) what he thinks the referent is.) The relationship between y─Бh├н and y├│toс╕е might be clearer if the rel. clause were tr. тАЬтАж never has the power to keep away.тАЭ On y├│toс╕е see now also Keydana (Inf., 77-78), who does not consider it a true infinitive. He takes y├бsya simply as the determiner of a gen. action noun y├│tu-. I am more inclined to see y├│tuс╕е as an infinitive, and therefore consider y├бsya as an example of тАЬattractionтАЭ to the case of the infinitive from an underlying obj. *y├бm.

The dative to the same stem does function as an infinitive and takes acc. rection: VIII.71.15 agn├нm dv├йс╣гo y├│tavai no gс╣Ыс╣З─лmasi (cf. VIII.18.5 dv├йс╣г─Бс╣Гsi y├│tave).

Griffith

With wealth, by thousand paths come hither, Agni, paths that bring ample strength, O thou Most Splendid.
Come, Son of Strength, o’er whom, Invoked of many! the godless hath no power to keep thee distant.

Geldner

Komm herw├дrts, Indra, auf tausend Wegen, die viel Gewinn bringen, mit Reichtum, du Glanzreicher, du Sohn der St├дrke, Vielgerufener, den niemals ein Ungott abzuwehren vermag!

Grassmann

Komm her auf tausend segensreichen Pfaden mit reichem Gut, o g├╝terreicher Indra, Komm, Sohn der Kraft, dem kein Gottloser jemals zu widerstehn vermochte, vielgerufner.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe vastness of the affluent, ancient (Indra), the demolisher (of foes), exceeds that of the heaven and the earth; there is no antagonist, no counterpart, no recipient of him abounding in wisdom, victorious (in war).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The greatness of the powerfully brilliant, stalwart, ardent one has overflowed from heaven and earth.
There exists no rival for him, nor counterpart, no opponent for the
strong one with many magical powers.

Griffith

From heaven, from earth is bruited forth the greatness of him the firm, the fiery, the resplendent.
No foe hath he, no counterpart, no refuge is there from him the Conqueror full of wisdom

Geldner

Grassmann

Weit ├╝ber Erd’ und Himmel ragt die Gr├╢sse des wilderregten, tapfern, g├╝terreichen; Kein Feind ist ihm gewachsen, nichts vergleichbar, kein Widerstand dem sehr gewandten Sieger.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThat exploit is celebrated in the present day (which you have) achieved for Kutsa, for ─Аyu, for Atithigvave; to him you have given many thousands (of riches), and you have quickly elevated Turvay─Бс╣Зa over the earth by your power.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Turvay_с╣Зa: same as Divod─Бsa, to whom Indra gave the spoils of ┼Ъambara

Jamison Brereton

This deed done by you stands out todayтАФthat for his sake
[=T┼лrvay─Бс╣ЗaтАЩs?] (you ground down) Kutsa, ─Аyu, and Atithigva;
many thousands did you grind down to earth. You led T┼лrvay─Бс╣Зa up boldly.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is structurally reminiscent of vs. 8. Like there, we have a clause occupying the first p─Бda (both ending in bh┼л╠Бt/bh┼лt, as it happens), with (most of) b belonging to a different but radically incomplete clause, containing a marooned set of accusative PNs whose fate at the hands of Indra is well known. P─Бda c continues with other accusative victims of Indra, but also provides a verb to govern them. In both vss. the names in the b clause have a well-known and quite specific outcome at IndraтАЩs hands: Cumuri and Dhuni in 8b were put to sleep by Indra, to weaken them for a death blow administered by someone else; as for our vs., acdg. to I.53.10 Indra made Kutsa, ─Аyu, and Atithigva subject (arandhan─Бyaс╕е) to T┼лrvay─Бс╣Зa, who also appears by name in our p─Бda d. In both 8b and 13b the published translation follows the same strategy: co-opting the verb in c (vс╣Ыс╣З├бk in 8, n├н ┼Ыi┼Ы─Бс╕е in 13) to govern not only the accusatives in its own p─Бda but also those in p─Бda b. This is syntactically a bit more complex in our vs. because b is a relative clause (with y├бd) so the unaccented verb of c cannot be applied to it directly. I still think this is the correct strategy in 8 and probably also here as well, but the presence of dat. asmai in b along with its likely referent t┼л╠Бrvay─Бс╣Зam in d makes me wonder if Geldner (n. 13b) may be right in simply supplying the verb found in the very phrase in I.53.10 tv├бm asmai k├║tsam atithigv├бm ─Бy├║m, тАж arandhan─Бyaс╕е, despite the isolation of that passage and its distance from ours. (Alternatively we could use ├бrdayaс╕е, which governs the same three names in VIII.53.2, but there is no dat. there; and it is likewise isolated and distant.) Oldenberg (both ZDMG 55.323 and Noten) is also in favor of supplying such a verb. Note in passing that unaccented asyai in our b presupposes a referent already in the discourse, so it must be anticipating t┼л╠Бrvay─Бс╣Зam in d. For T┼лrvay─Бс╣Зa cf. the simile t┼л╠Бrvan n├б y─Б╠Бman in nearby VI.15.5 with disc. ad loc.

Griffith

This day the deed that thou hast done is famous, when thou, for him, with many thousand others
Laidest low Kutsa, Ayu, Atithigva, and boldly didst deliver Turvayana.

Geldner

Dieses dein getanes Werk soll noch heute gelten, da├Я du ihm den Kutsa, Ayu, Atithigva ├╝berantwortetest. Viele Tausende stachst du zu Boden; dem Turvayana hast du mutig herausgeholfen.

Grassmann

Heut steh voran dies Werk, das du vollbrachtest, dass du den Kutsa, Aju, Atithigwa Zu Boden strecktest viele tausend diesem Turvajana und k├╝hn heraus ihn f├╝hrtest.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDivine Indra, all the gods have glorified you, the wisest of the wise, for the destruction of Ahi; when propitiated, you have given wealth to the distressed worshipper, and to his posterity.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

When propitiated: yatra varivo b─Бdhit─Бya dive jan─Бya tanve gс╣Ыс╣Зaс╕е karaс╕е = yasmin k─Бle piditya stotre jan─Бya tat tanay─Бya ca dhanam st┼лyam─Бс╣Зo adadaс╕е = when being praised, you have given ease to the celestial people through the relief, tanve, ┼Ыobh─Бyai, caused by the demolition of Ahi

Jamison Brereton

Then, o god, all the gods cheer you on for the serpent-smashing, (you) the best poet of poets,
when you will create wide space for oppressed heaven, for its people and for yourself as you are being sung.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The aor. subjunctive k├бraс╕е is generally taken as preterital, an interpr.

licensed by Grassmann, who identifies it as тАЬImpf.тАЭ But this is morphologically irresponsible, and further, given the injunc. m├бdan in the main cl. (b), a proper subj. value is quite possible. I think this is an example of the standard rhetorical move to take IndraтАЩs signal mythological deeds and make them a model for his behavior in the future, to our benefit. The next and final vs. continues this point of view. See Hoffmann (Injunk. 55 and n. 37) for a similar assessment, though he also envisions the possibility of тАЬKonjunktiv im pr├дteritalen Sachverhalt.тАЭ

Griffith

In thee, O God, the wisest of the Sages, all Gods were joyful when thou slewest Ahi.
When lauded for thyself, thou gavest freedom to sore-afflicted Heaven and to the people.

English translation:

тАЬThe heaven and earth, and the immortal gods, acknowledge your might; doer of many deeds, do that which is yet undone by you, give birth to a new hymn at (your) sacrifice.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Heaven and Earth and the immortal gods give way to your
might, Indra.
Do, o doer, what undone (deed) exists for you (to do). Generate a newer hymn for yourself along with sacrifices.

Griffith

This power of thine both heaven and earth acknowledge, the deathless Gods acknowledge it, O Indra.
Do what thou ne’er hast done, O Mighty Worker: beget a new hymn at thy sacrifices.

Geldner

Grassmann

Es gaben, Indra, dieser deiner St├дrke die ew’gen G├╢tter, Himmel nach und Erde; O thue, th├дt’ger, was noch ungethan ist, erzeuge neues Lob dir durch die Opfer.

(рддреЗ) рдЖрдкрдХреЗ рд╕рдореАрдк рд╕реЗ рдЬреЛ (рдЕрдорд░реНрддреНрдпрд╛рдГ) рд╕рд╛рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡ рд╕реЗ рд╡рд┐рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдг рд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЬрди (рдпрддреН) рдЬреЛ (рдЕрдХреГрддрдореН) рдирд╣реАрдВ рдХрд┐рдпрд╛ рдЧрдпрд╛ рдХрд░реНрдо рдФрд░ (рдирд╡реАрдпрдГ) рдЕрддрд┐рд╢рдп рдирд╡реАрди рд╡рдЪрди (рдЙрдХреНрдердореН) рдХрд╣рдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп (рдЕрд╕реНрддрд┐) рд╣реИ (рддрддреН) рдЙрд╕ (рддреЗ) рдЖрдкрдХреЗ рд╡рдЪрди рдХреЛ (рдЬрд┐рд╣рддреЗ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддреЗ рдФрд░ (рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА) рднреВрдорд┐ рдФрд░ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдХреЛ (рдЕрдиреБ) рдкрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рдЙрдирдХреЛ рдЖрдк (рдпрдЬреНрдЮреИрдГ) рдореЗрд▓ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд░реВрдк рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░реЛрдВ рд╕реЗ (рдЬрдирдпрд╕реНрд╡) рдкреНрд░рдХрдЯ рдХреАрдЬрд┐рдпреЗ рдФрд░ (рдУрдЬрдГ) рдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдо рдХреЛ (рдХреГрд╖реНрд╡рд╛) рдХрд░рд┐рдпреЗ реерезрелрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ ! рдЖрдк рд▓реЛрдЧ рднреВрдорд┐ рдФрд░ рдмрд┐рдЬреБрд▓реА рдЖрджрд┐ рдХреА рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рд╕реЗ рдирд╡реАрди-рдирд╡реАрди рдХрд╛рд░реНрдп рдХреЛ рд╕рд┐рджреНрдз рдХрд░рд┐рдпреЗ реерезрелрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░, рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдФрд░ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрди рдХрд░рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдЗрд╕рд╕реЗ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ рдЕрдард╛рд░рд╣рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рдЫрдард╛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдХреГрддреНрдиреЛ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ ! рддреЗ рддрд╡ рд╕рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рджреНрдпреЗрд╜рдорд░реНрддреНрдпрд╛ рджреЗрд╡рд╛ рдпрджрдХреГрддрдВ рдирд╡реАрдп рдЙрдХреНрдердорд╕реНрддрд┐ рддрддреНрддреЗ рдЬрд┐рд╣рддреЗ рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА рдЕрдиреБ рдЬрд┐рд╣рддреЗ рддрд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮреИрд░реНрдЬрдирдпрд╕реНрд╡реЛрдЬрдГ рдХреГрд╖реНрд╡рд╛ реерезрелрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд░реНрдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреИрдГ рдХрд┐рдВ рдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╡реНрдпрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрдиреБ) (рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА) рднреВрдорд┐рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпреМ (рддрддреН) (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рдУрдЬрдГ) рдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдордореН (рдЕрдорд░реНрддреНрдпрд╛рдГ) рд╕рд╛рдзрд╛рд░рдгрдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рджреНрд╡рд┐рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рдГ (рдЬрд┐рд╣рддреЗ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рд░рд╛рдЬрдиреН (рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ) (рдХреГрд╖реНрд╡рд╛) рдХреБрд░реБрд╖реНрд╡ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рджреНрд╡реНрдпрдЪреЛрд╜рддрд╕реНрддрд┐рдЩ рдЗрддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред (рдХреГрддреНрдиреЛ) рдХрд░реНрддреНрддрдГ (рдЕрдХреГрддрдореН) рдЕрдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрдорд╛рдгрдВ рдХрд░реНрдореНрдо (рдпрддреН) (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рдЕрд╕реНрддрд┐) (рдЙрдХреНрдердореН) рд╡рдХреНрддреБрдорд░реНрд╣рдореН (рдирд╡реАрдпрдГ) рдЕрддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрди рдиреВрддрдирдВ рд╡рдЪрдирдореН (рдЬрдирдпрд╕реНрд╡) (рдпрдЬреНрдЮреИрдГ) рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рдордпреИрд░реНрд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░реИрдГ реерезрелрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ ! рдпреВрдпрдВ рднреВрдорд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрджрд╛рджрд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдпрд╛ рдирд╡реАрдирдВ рдирд╡реАрдирдВ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрдВ рд╕рд╛рдзреНрдиреБрддреЗрддрд┐ реерезрелрее рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрд░рд╛рдЬрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддреНрдпрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рджрд╢рдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╖рд╖реНрдареЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ
